        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271224790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15131265531808033053">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>3 years ago, Alison went missing. Nobody knows what happened to her, but now 3 years later, her 4 closest friends start receiving strange messages. Messages that say things that only Alison would know, messages that are signed simply A.<br/>Is Alison really back? Who else could the messages really be from? And if Alison really is back, what does she want?<br/><br/><br/>I watched the first season of this as a TV show and really liked it, but never got around to reading the books. </span>
  <span id="freeText15131265531808033053" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />3 years ago, Alison went missing. Nobody knows what happened to her, but now 3 years later, her 4 closest friends start receiving strange messages. Messages that say things that only Alison would know, messages that are signed simply A.<br />Is Alison really back? Who else could the messages really be from? And if Alison really is back, what does she want?<br /><br /><br />I watched the first season of this as a TV show and really liked it, but never got around to reading the books. I’m so glad I read this one now though ‘cause it was awesome!<br /><br />I always think it’s a bit of a gamble reading a book that has been turned into a movie or TV series, as often one will leave you disappointed. Thankfully this wasn’t one of those books!<br />Firstly I liked the writing in this book, and it seemed really similar to the TV show, so whoever did the crossover for the show did a really good job. I kinda felt like I already knew the characters as I had seen the TV show, and I think this actually made me like the book even more than I perhaps would have done, as I could imagine what was going on a lot better.<br /><br />The characters all seemed really similar to those in the TV show, although I did think that they seemed maybe a little more friendlier in the TV show than in the book. I also thought that the book maybe didn’t cover as much ground as the first season of the show? But I really can’t remember so I could be miles off here.<br /><br />I liked the storyline. I thought the mystery over who A. really was really compelling, and I loved trying to guess what would happen next. I couldn’t really remember much about the TV show, but as I was reading through this book, something would happen and I would think ‘I remember that now!’ but because I couldn’t remember it initially, this helped keep the mystery in the story.<br />I have to say that I was quite shocked by what the girls got up to in this story though. We had shoplifting, drinking, affairs with teachers, and all sorts of other stuff, which was pretty crazy, but at the same time really good!<br />I thought that this book did end in a good place, but there were still so many questions and mysteries unanswered that I really just want to dive into the next one straight away!<br />Overall; a great YA contemporary mystery.<br />9 out of 10.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15131265531808033053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_672569006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/672569006" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/672569006?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/11816548-pretty-little-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=just-couldn-t-finish">just-couldn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer672569006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3807087435069613470">It wouldn’t be fair for me to rate this book. I’m not only not the correct target demographic — clearly tweens and teens — but I fall into the reviled substrata of the novel: earnest smart girl. I don’t know how much I would have liked the book at 15, much less at 55. If you hated — just hated — high school, chances are that mean girls like these were the reason why.<br/><br/>The novel begins with an alliance amongst five seventh-grade students who become the mean girls clique of Rosewood Day School, loca</span>
  <span id="freeText3807087435069613470" style="display:none">It wouldn’t be fair for me to rate this book. I’m not only not the correct target demographic — clearly tweens and teens — but I fall into the reviled substrata of the novel: earnest smart girl. I don’t know how much I would have liked the book at 15, much less at 55. If you hated — just hated — high school, chances are that mean girls like these were the reason why.<br /><br />The novel begins with an alliance amongst five seventh-grade students who become the mean girls clique of Rosewood Day School, located in a thinly veiled Bucks County, Pennsylvania. The leader of the pack, Allison DiLaurentis, the meanest of the girls, disappears suddenly, and the clique dissolves. But the four remaining girls — Spencer Hastings, Hanna Marin, Aria Montgomery and Emily Fields — continue as shallow as ever; indeed, no hermit was ever as devoted to God as these girls are to Abercrombie &amp; Fitch. They’re self-centered to the point of narcissism with a breath-taking sense of entitlement, and haven’t a clue as to the lives of the average American. They’re virtually a parody of the progeny of the 1 percent. Occupy Wall Street couldn’t come up with cruder poster children for the evils of economic inequality.<br /><br />Soon after the girls embark on their junior year, Allison’s corpse turns up, but the quartet begin receiving threatening text messages from “A.” Has Allison’s ghost returned for revenge? Emily, Hanna, Aria and Spencer — especially Emily — have terrible secrets that would ruin their lives. Is there an “A” who hates Allison and her former posse enough to reveal their secrets? Or is “A” one of the girls themselves? After all, who but the five of them knew these secrets?<br /><br />To tell the truth, I just couldn’t make myself care. The premise — texts from beyond the grave, so to speak — seemed quite intriguing. With a more likeable group of girls, I know I could well have enjoyed this book. But the eponymous <i>Pretty Little Liars</i> had more in common with the usual cruel villains of a novel than the protagonists. <br /><br />You know who you are: As my friend Emily Erkan used to say, If you like this kind of thing, this is just the kind of thing you’d like. Just count me out.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3807087435069613470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2850242281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2850242281" />
    <a title="Corinne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43631160-corinne"><img alt="Corinne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504392619p2/43631160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2850242281?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corinne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corinne" href="/user/show/43631160-corinne">Corinne</a>
      </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841813597" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6919017766822609918"><b>
  <i>Pretty Little Liars by Sara Shepard</i>
</b><br/><br/>I absolutely <u>LOVE</u> the Pretty Little Liars TV show, and when that show first started i wasn't a crazy reader, but i bought the first 8 books of this series. As the years went on i never thought i'd actually read them. I'll admit its taken me SO long to finally pick up this book and separate my TV thoughts from the book, but I'm so glad i picked it up!<br/><br/>I was so pleasantly surprised by this book! I really enjoyed it.<br/>I loved how each chapter was focused on a dif</span>
  <span id="freeText6919017766822609918" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Pretty Little Liars by Sara Shepard</i>
</b><br /><br />I absolutely <u>LOVE</u> the Pretty Little Liars TV show, and when that show first started i wasn't a crazy reader, but i bought the first 8 books of this series. As the years went on i never thought i'd actually read them. I'll admit its taken me SO long to finally pick up this book and separate my TV thoughts from the book, but I'm so glad i picked it up!<br /><br />I was so pleasantly surprised by this book! I really enjoyed it.<br />I loved how each chapter was focused on a different character, that's really unique and so fun, it also allows you not to get bored of one storyline for too long.<br />The only things i didn't like about this book was that the 4 main girls really threw themselves at guys. I hope this changes as the books go on and the characters develop :)<br /><br />Im quite excited to read the second book of the series, and hope i'll want to continue on with the entire <s>extremely long</s> series! <br /><br />P.S: If anyones interested, i have a Pretty Little Liars and Vampire Diaries Instagram account: @PrettyLittleLyingVampires, if you want to follow :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="6919017766822609918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2587775250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2682452776190112858">Confession: I was not a regular watcher of this show, but my sister binged it and I would see episodes now and then so my interest was piqued to get the full story.<br/><br/>My biggest takeaway is how freaking happy I am to NOT be the mother of any of these characters because they are ALL bad as crap. You may be thinking that SOMEONE has to be a good kid. No... Not in this story, at least not in the entirety of book one. <br/><br/>Is this book amazing? No. Is it pretty young minded? Yes. Was it still fun to read? Y</span>
  <span id="freeText2682452776190112858" style="display:none">Confession: I was not a regular watcher of this show, but my sister binged it and I would see episodes now and then so my interest was piqued to get the full story.<br /><br />My biggest takeaway is how freaking happy I am to NOT be the mother of any of these characters because they are ALL bad as crap. You may be thinking that SOMEONE has to be a good kid. No... Not in this story, at least not in the entirety of book one. <br /><br />Is this book amazing? No. Is it pretty young minded? Yes. Was it still fun to read? Yes. Will I continue on with the series? Yes, it's not a binge read type of book for me, but when I need something that I can laugh at AND be appalled at simultaneously, this is definitely in my choices. <br /><br />Favorite quote: "Ezra had come up with the lamest excuse for swearing in class.”I was afraid that a bee had flown into my pants, and I thought the bee was going to sting me, and so I yelled out in terror."<br /><br />Caution: There are a lot of teen issues addressed in this book. Such as weight issues/bulimia, underage drinking, drug use, drunk driving, bullying, statutory rape, etc.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10024356803915195934">This has been on my list for a while, and I'm glad to have finally read it, but I guess it just isn't really my thing. The whole rich-girl-does-bad-things storyline feels a bit overused and the part that actually is the most annoying is that there is no solution at the end of this to the mystery that is meant to be central to the book.<br/>I guess I'm just not the target market.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VPzembVdqWRNE3dY6/uergJcczeilEBuJc0J8TGA31Fu2rdLDgNgDOo4wzkcDpRx1AOU/2wZzgl+s09A/MMtyw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gTUQw1CMa7fXDAa5m98/ujqFtzk7B9M2s9gyDUxpVJy7E3kR69Ki33AnsthsKjVl7NpQ8fWKXVHopnS8gSqmBg==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer7896435558522578523">Sara Shepard graduated from NYU and has an MFA from Brooklyn College. She has lived in New York City, Brooklyn, Tucson, Arizona, Philadelphia, and now lives in Pittsburgh, PA. Sara's Pretty Little Liars novels were inspired by her upbringing in Philadelphia's Main Line.</span>
